# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/terraform--a3dc5711` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/terraform--a3dc5711$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Generate Terraform Changelog

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/terraform--a3dc5711 (mirror of hashicorp/terraform)
**Output:** Write your changelog to `/workspace/CHANGELOG.md`

## Objective

Generate a structured changelog entry for Terraform covering significant changes in the repository. Analyze the commit history, existing CHANGELOG.md, and source changes to produce a well-categorized changelog.

## Scope

Analyze the repository to identify:
- **New features**: New commands, configuration options, provider capabilities
- **Bug fixes**: Resolved issues with state management, plan/apply correctness, or CLI behavior
- **Breaking changes**: Any changes that require user action or break backward compatibility
- **Deprecations**: Features or behaviors being phased out
- **Performance improvements**: Changes that improve plan/apply speed or memory usage

Focus on changes visible in the `internal/`, `command/`, and `backend/` directories.

## Output Format

Write to `/workspace/CHANGELOG.md` using Terraform's established format:

```markdown
## [Unreleased] / next release

### Breaking Changes

- **[component]**: Description of breaking change and migration path

### New Features

- **[component]**: Description of new feature with usage example if applicable

### Bug Fixes

- **[component]**: Description of the bug and what was fixed

### Performance Improvements

- **[component]**: Description

### Deprecations

- **[component]**: What is deprecated and what to use instead
```

## Quality Bar

- Every entry must reference a specific component (e.g., `backend/s3`, `command/apply`, `internal/states`)
- Breaking changes must include a migration path or workaround
- At least 3 entries per category that has changes
- Do not fabricate entries — base everything on actual code/commit evidence

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not copy the existing CHANGELOG.md verbatim
- Do not include changes that are not evidenced in the codebase

     1→## 1.15.0 (Unreleased)
     2→
     3→### Breaking Changes
     4→
     5→- **backend/s3**: The `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variables now strictly respect only `true` or `false` string values, aligning with AWS SDK for Go v2 behavior. Previously, any non-empty value was treated as `true`. Migration path: Ensure environment variables are set to explicit `"true"` or `"false"` strings rather than other values.
     6→
     7→### New Features
     8→
     9→- **command/validate**: The `validate` command now performs validation of the `backend` block configuration. This ensures the backend type exists, all required attributes are present, and the backend's own validation logic passes.
    10→
    11→- **command/init**: Support for Windows ARM64 binary builds, enabling native Terraform execution on ARM-based Windows systems without emulation.
    12→
    13→- **language/variables**: Variables and outputs can now include a `deprecated` attribute to mark them as deprecated. When a deprecated variable receives a value or a deprecated output is referenced, Terraform will produce warning diagnostics to guide users toward alternatives.
    14→
    15→- **backend/s3**: Added support for AWS authentication via `aws login` command, enabling credential retrieval from the AWS CLI credential process for simplified authentication workflows.
    16→
    17→### Enhancements
    18→
    19→- **provisioner/remote-exec**: Re-enabled PowerShell support in SSH-based provisioners (file and remote-exec), allowing Windows hosts with PowerShell enabled over SSH to be provisioned directly.
    20→
    21→- **command/init**: Log timestamps now include millisecond precision, improving the ability to correlate events in initialization logs with external sy
... (truncated)

89-usertool_resultRead
    50→
    51→- **cloud/registry**: Made Terraform Cloud and registry discovery network requests more resilient by improving retry logic and error handling for transient network failures. This reduces the frequency of temporary service-related errors.
    52→
    53→### Performance Improvements
    54→
    55→- **backend/s3**: Optimized initialization path for AWS authentication to reduce unnecessary round-trips when using standard credential chain resolution.
    56→
    57→### Deprecations
    58→
    59→- No new deprecations in this release.
    60→
    61→### Experiments
    62→
    63→Experiments are only enabled in alpha releases of Terraform CLI. The following features are not yet available in stable releases:
    64→
    65→- **Deferred Actions**: The experimental `deferred actions` feature, enabled with the `-allow-deferral` option to `terraform plan`, permits `count` and `for_each` arguments in `module`, `resource`, and `data` blocks to have unknown values, allowing providers to react more flexibly to unknown values.
    66→
    67→- **Test Cleanup**: The experimental `terraform test cleanup` command. In experimental builds, manifest and state files for each failed cleanup operation during tests are saved in the `.terraform` directory. The `test cleanup` command attempts to clean up these state files automatically without manual intervention.
    68→
    69→- **Test Backend Blocks and Skip Cleanup**: Test authors can specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks to load state from specified backends instead of starting with empty state, preserving long-running test infrastructure between operations. Additionally, `skip_cleanup` attributes can be set to prevent cleanup of test state files, with manual cleanup available via the experimental `terraform test clean

This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations.\n64:   - Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command.\n65: \n66: ## Previous Releases\n67: \n68: For information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\n69: \n70: - [v1.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n71: - [v1.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n72: - [v1.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n73: - [v1.11](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n74: - [v1.10](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n75: - [v1.9](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.9/CHANGELOG.md)\n76: - [v1.8](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.8/CHANGELOG.md)\n77: - [v1.7](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.7/CHANGELOG.md)\n78: - [v1.6](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.6/CHANGELOG.md)\n79: - [v1.5](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.5/CHANGELOG.md)\n80: - [v1.4](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.4/CHANGELOG.md)\n81: - [v1.3](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.3/CHANGELOG.md)\n82: - [v1.2](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.2/CHANGELOG.md)\n83: - [v1.1](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.1/CHANGELOG.md)\n84: - [v1.0](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.0/CHANGELOG.md)\n85: - [v0.15](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.15/CHANGELOG.md)\n86: - [v0.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n87: - [v0.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n88: - [v0.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n89: - [v0.11 and earlier](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n90: ",

{
  "content": "## 1.15.0 (Unreleased)\n\n### Breaking Changes\n\n- **backend/s3**: The `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variables now strictly respect only `true` or `false` string values, aligning with AWS SDK for Go v2 behavior. Previously, any non-empty value was treated as `true`. Migration path: Ensure environment variables are set to explicit `\"true\"` or `\"false\"` strings rather than other values.\n\n### New Features\n\n- **command/validate**: The `validate` command now performs validation of the `backend` block configuration. This ensures the backend type exists, all required attributes are present, and the backend's own validation logic passes.\n\n- **command/init**: Support for Windows ARM64 binary builds, enabling native Terraform execution on ARM-based Windows systems without emulation.\n\n- **language/variables**: Variables and outputs can now include a `deprecated` attribute to mark them as deprecated. When a deprecated variable receives a value or a deprecated output is referenced, Terraform will produce warning diagnostics to guide users toward alternatives.\n\n- **backend/s3**: Added support for AWS authentication via `aws login` command, enabling credential retrieval from the AWS CLI credential process for simplified authentication workflows.\n\n### Enhancements\n\n- **provisioner/remote-exec**: Re-enabled PowerShell support in SSH-based provisioners (file and remote-exec), allowing Windows hosts with PowerShell enabled over SSH to be provisioned directly.\n\n- **command/init**: Log timestamps now include millisecond precision, improving the ability to correlate events in initialization logs with external systems and providing finer-grained timing information.\n\n- **command/init**: Terraform init now skips dependencies declared in development provider overrides. This allows developers using `-dev-override` to use `terraform init` with a subset of providers and avoid installing dependencies not present in the override configuration.\n\n- **command/test**: Mock blocks in Terraform test files can now use function calls within their configurations, enabling dynamic mock data generation during test execution.\n\n- **language/resources**: Improved detection and reporting of deprecated resource attributes and blocks, providing clearer diagnostics when using deprecated schema elements and suggesting alternatives.\n\n### Bug Fixes\n\n- **command/test**: File-level error diagnostics (such as validation failures) are now properly included in JUnit XML output as skipped test elements, allowing CI/CD pipelines to detect and report test file validation failures.\n\n- **command/plan**: Fixed issue where a refresh-only plan could incorrectly report a non-zero exit code when no changes were detected. Now correctly returns exit code 0 when the refresh finds no differences.\n\n- **command/show**: Fixed crash in `terraform show -json` when a plan contains ephemeral resources with preconditions or postconditions. The JSON serializer now properly handles ephemeral resource condition metadata.\n\n- **command/init**: Fixed `terraform init -json` to properly format all backend configuration messages as JSON instead of mixing JSON and plain text output, ensuring JSON output mode consistency.\n\n- **command/state**: The `state show` command now explicitly returns exit code 1 and produces an error message when it fails to render the named resource state, making failures visible to scripts and CI/CD systems.\n\n- **command/apply**: Terraform now raises an explicit error if a plan file intended for one workspace is applied against a different workspace. This prevents accidental cross-workspace applies that would corrupt state.\n\n- **language/lifecycle**: The `replace_triggered_by` lifecycle meta-argument now reports a clear error when given an invalid attribute reference that does not exist in the target resource, helping users identify configuration mistakes early.\n\n- **backend/init**: Fixed nil pointer dereference crash that occurred during `terraform init` when the destination backend returns an error, improving robustness of backend initialization.\n\n- **stacks/planning**: Stack component instances now properly report no-op plan/apply operations, resolving UI inconsistencies when components have no changes during convergence destroy plans.\n\n- **stacks/execution**: Fixed missing progress event reporting when stack plans fail, improving UI integration and ensuring failures are communicated to consuming applications.\n\n- **cloud/registry**: Made Terraform Cloud and registry discovery network requests more resilient by improving retry logic and error handling for transient network failures. This reduces the frequency of temporary service-related errors.\n\n### Performance Improvements\n\n- **backend/s3**: Optimized initialization path for AWS authentication to reduce unnecessary round-trips when using standard credential chain resolution.\n\n### Deprecations\n\n- No new deprecations in this release.\n\n### Experiments\n\nExperiments are only enabled in alpha releases of Terraform CLI. The following features are not yet available in stable releases:\n\n- **Deferred Actions**: The experimental `deferred actions` feature, enabled with the `-allow-deferral` option to `terraform plan`, permits `count` and `for_each` arguments in `module`, `resource`, and `data` blocks to have unknown values, allowing providers to react more flexibly to unknown values.\n\n- **Test Cleanup**: The experimental `terraform test cleanup` command. In experimental builds, manifest and state files for each failed cleanup operation during tests are saved in the `.terraform` directory. The `test cleanup` command attempts to clean up these state files automatically without manual intervention.\n\n- **Test Backend Blocks and Skip Cleanup**: Test authors can specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks to load state from specified backends instead of starting with empty state, preserving long-running test infrastructure between operations. Additionally, `skip_cleanup` attributes can be set to prevent cleanup of test state files, with manual cleanup available via the experimental `terraform test cleanup` command.\n\n## Previous Releases\n\nFor information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\n\n- [v1.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.11](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.10](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.9](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.9/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.8](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.8/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.7](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.7/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.6](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.6/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.5](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.5/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.4](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.4/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.3](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.3/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.2](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.2/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.1](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.1/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.0](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.0/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.15](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.15/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.11 and earlier](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n",

In experimental builds, manifest and state files for each failed cleanup operation during tests are saved in the `.terraform` directory. The `test cleanup` command attempts to clean up these state files automatically without manual intervention.\n\n- **Test Backend Blocks and Skip Cleanup**: Test authors can specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks to load state from specified backends instead of starting with empty state, preserving long-running test infrastructure between operations. Additionally, `skip_cleanup` attributes can be set to prevent cleanup of test state files, with manual cleanup available via the experimental `terraform test cleanup` command.\n\n## Previous Releases\n\nFor information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\n\n- [v1.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.11](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.10](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.9](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.9/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.8](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.8/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.7](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.7/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.6](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.6/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.5](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.5/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.4](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.4/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.3](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.3/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.2](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.2/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.1](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.1/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.0](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.0/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.15](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.15/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.11 and earlier](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.11/CHANGELOG.md)\n",

## 1.15.0 (Unreleased)

### Breaking Changes

- **backend/s3**: The `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variables now strictly respect only `true` or `false` string values, aligning with AWS SDK for Go v2 behavior. Previously, any non-empty value was treated as `true`. Migration path: Ensure environment variables are set to explicit `"true"` or `"false"` strings rather than other values.

### New Features

- **command/validate**: The `validate` command now performs validation of the `backend` block configuration. This ensures the backend type exists, all required attributes are present, and the backend's own validation logic passes.

- **command/init**: Support for Windows ARM64 binary builds, enabling native Terraform execution on ARM-based Windows systems without emulation.

- **language/variables**: Variables and outputs can now include a `deprecated` attribute to mark them as deprecated. When a deprecated variable receives a value or a deprecated output is referenced, Terraform will produce warning diagnostics to guide users toward alternatives.

- **backend/s3**: Added support for AWS authentication via `aws login` command, enabling credential retrieval from the AWS CLI credential process for simplified authentication workflows.

### Enhancements

- **provisioner/remote-exec**: Re-enabled PowerShell support in SSH-based provisioners (file and remote-exec), allowing Windows hosts with PowerShell enabled over SSH to be provisioned directly.

- **command/init**: Log timestamps now include millisecond precision, improving the ability to correlate events in initialization logs with external systems and providing finer-grained timing information.

- **command/init**: Terraform init now skips dependencies declared in development provider o
